The Secrets of&nbsp;Scientology</h1> 							<div class="entry-meta"> 					<span class="meta-prep meta-prep-author">Posted on</span> <a href="https://markrathbun.wordpress.com/2010/09/28/bbc-panorama-the-secrets-of-scientology/" title="11:20 pm" rel="bookmark"><span class="entry-date">September 28, 2010</span></a> <span class="by-author"><span class="sep">by</span> <span class="author vcard"><a class="url fn n" href="https://markrathbun.wordpress.com/author/martyrathbun09/" title="View all posts by Mark C. Rathbun" rel="author">Mark C. Rathbun</a></span> </span><span class="comments-link"><span class="meta-sep">|</span> <a href="https://markrathbun.wordpress.com/2010/09/28/bbc-panorama-the-secrets-of-scientology/#comments">522 Comments</a></span> 									</div><!-- .entry-meta --> 			 			<div class="entry-content"> 				<p>Well, that is the title in any event.  In fact,  the secrets they promised to tell never made it into the final edit. You can thank David Miscavige if you got the overall impression Scientology itself is weird.  The fifty letters from the Church and its lawyers to the BBC  that the church brags about in its counter video promised litigation should those secrets be told .  In other words, spend parishioner donations to cover Dave&#8217;s ass exclusively, forcing the media to fill in with old hat, more generalized attack material.  Protect Miscavige at the expense of Scientology.   </p> <p>The show does give credible accounts from Mike, Amy, Marc, Claire, Jason, Mareka, et al on matters the world ought to know.  But, the secrets that were touted and would have had the most salutory effects were left on the editing room floor.</p> <p>In that respect, I admit I was wrong. I earlier suggested the BBC would be less inclined to back off as I had accused U.S. media of doing (since the BBC is publicly funded).   At the end of the day, I remain confident that the &#8216;save Dave at any expense&#8217; strategy will be his own undoing.</p> <span class='embed-youtube' style='text-align:center; display: block;'><iframe class='youtube-player' type='text/html' width='500' height='312' src='https://www.youtube.com/embed/l42UrHDx4lE?version=3&#038;rel=1&#038;fs=1&#038;showsearch=0&#038;showinfo=1&#038;iv_load_policy=1&#038;wmode=transparent' frameborder='0' allowfullscreen='true'></iframe></span> <span class='embed-youtube' style='text-align:center; display: block;'><iframe class='youtube-player' type='text/html' width='500' height='312' "3485" )' aria-label='Reply to Han Solo'>Reply</a>								</span><!-- .comment-meta .commentmetadata --> 		</div><!-- .comment-author .vcard --> 		 		<div class="comment-body"><p>Well, the concept of spiritual entities influencing people isn&#8217;t really new.</p> <p>In 1924 a psychiatrist oublished a book to reform psychiatry. He had discovered that his patients were suffering from such entities. He was able to transfer these from the patient to another person &#8211; the patient got well and the other person suffered now from the patient&#8217;s symptoms. </p> <p>And he developed a therapy to finally heal these entities by increasing their awareness, resulting in no one suffering from them any more.</p> <p>He was some 200 years ahead of psychiatry of course, so his methods were not accepted.</p> <p>The book is &#8220;30 years among the dead&#8221; by Carl Wickland. It has even been translated to German ( title : &#8220;30 Jahre unter den Toten&#8221; ) and is available here today.</p> </div>  	</div><!-- #comment-##  -->  	<ul class="children"> 	<li For example, in the 17th century, Leibniz arrived at an explanation of reality that includes a source of force called a &#8220;monad&#8221;. Monads are defined as nonmaterial metaphysical entities that resemble souls.  Leibniz thought that they are the source of all activity that accompanied matter.<br /> If you want to learn more, Wikipedia is no good on this subject. You have to go to history books and other academic materials.</p> </div>  	</div><!-- #comment-##  -->  	</li><!-- #comment-## --> 	<li class="comment odd alt depth-5 highlander-comment" id="li-comment-52535"> 		<div id="comment-52535"> 		<div class="comment-author vcard"> 			<img alt='' src='https://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a27cf4e97e40e758ca5646b62b3d6283?s=48&#038;d=identicon&#038;r=G' class='avatar avatar-48' height='48' width='48' /> 			<cite class="fn">Lord Of The Undead</cite>  			<span class="comment-meta commentmetadata"> 				| 				<a href="https://markrathbun.wordpress.com/2010/09/28/bbc-panorama-the-secrets-of-scientology/#comment-52535"> 				September 29, 2010 at 3:46 pm</a> 					| 					<a class='comment-reply-link' href='/2010/09/28/bbc-panorama-the-secrets-of-scientology/?replytocom=52535#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-52535", "52535", "respond", "3485" )' aria-label='Reply to Lord Of The Undead'>Reply</a>								</span><!-- .comment-meta .commentmetadata --> 		</div><!-- .comment-author .vcard --> 		 		<div class="comment-body"><p>30 years among the dead. The malleable cult celebrities who are coached to ask rhetorical questions that aren’t the least bit rhetorical, e.g., Anne Archer&#8217;s faux furious snarl, &#8220;Do I look brainwashed to you?&#8221;  (Cringe!)</p> <p>2.  Cathy Rinder&#8217;s over-the-top shriekage, a dramatic contrast with her demure matron in the second row image on Anderson Cooper 360.   Those two images beg someone, anyone, please, to overlay her AC360 video footage with Sweeney’s phone recordings of her foul and hateful language.  </p> <p>3.  The regimentation and depersonalization of today’s Sea Org.</p> <p>4.  The cult’s obsession with respectability and ‘property portfolio’ (love that term).  </p> <p>5.  The relentless and arrogant harassment of those who found the courage to leave a cult they had joined as children to regain their sanity and freedom.  </p> <p>6.  The idiocy of confiding ANYTHING to an auditor or any other agent of the current-day ‘Church of Scientology’.</p> <p>7.  The homophobic and sadistic sexual obsessions of the self-anointed ‘Pope of Scientology’ – David Miscavige.  </p> <p>Happily, the program also demonstrated:  </p> <p>1.  The difference that three years away from RPF imprisonment can make – in Mike, who is so much happier, brighter, healthier and relaxed than he was in 2007.  </p> <p>2.  The contrast between Tommy Davis’s and Jan Eastgate’s covert hostility and the normal human affection and communication available from Marty, Amy, Mike, Claire, Marc, Jason.   </p> <p>3.  The high personal integrity and courage of every one of the Independent Scientologists and critics!  </p> <p>4.  The simple fact that Scientology philosophy and practices are valued and applied to good effect outside the cult. </p> <p>Tonight, the Internet is immensely more powerful than the cult’s lies.  Any ‘Secrets of Scientology’ not imparted through the Panorama program can be shared on this and other blogs.  Starting tomorrow, each of us can choose to start more conversations with loved ones and friends.  In those conversations, gradients and ARC apply, and active listening beats the hell out of sermonizing.  I had one of those conversations earlier this week.  The evidence against the cult is everywhere and will be seen when people choose to look.  </p> <p>I no longer wonder about when the cult will topple.  I don’t worry about its beautiful, empty buildings or its billions of dollars hidden in offshore bank accounts or David Miscavige’s tight grip on the church’s throat – nothing can prop it up.  The Church of Scientology is stone cold dead.  </p> <p>If Scientology survives, and I believe it will, it will do so in the sunshine, shared spontaneously among friends and disseminated freely on the Internet – not doled out as bait or sold as statuses or indulgences.  </p> <p>Thank you to everyone who contributed to this program.  I appreciate your efforts very much.  Everything will turn out fine.    </p> <p>Just Me</p> </div>  	</div><!-- #comment-##  -->  	<ul class="children"> 	<li class="comment byuser comment-author-mrinder odd alt depth-2 highlander-comment" id="li-comment-52482"> 		<div id="comment-52482"> 		<div class="comment-author vcard"> 			<img alt='' src='https://1.gravatar.com/avatar/ab01b94a5e488af57abff572315e5487?s=48&#038;d=identicon&#038;r=G' class='avatar avatar-48' height='48' width='48' /> 			<cite class="fn">mrinder</cite>  			<span class="comment-meta commentmetadata"> 				| 				<a href="https://markrathbun.wordpress.com/2010/09/28/bbc-panorama-the-secrets-of-scientology/#comment-52482"> 				September 29, 2010 at 10:14 am</a> 					| 					<a class='comment-reply-link' href='/2010/09/28/bbc-panorama-the-secrets-of-scientology/?replytocom=52482#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-52482", "52482", "respond", "3485" )' aria-label='Reply to mrinder'>Reply</a>								</span><!-- .comment-meta .commentmetadata --> 		</div><!-- .comment-author .vcard --> 		 		<div class="comment-body"><p>Thanks JM. I think people have the right to know what&#8217;s being sold. You may not think so, but I do.</p> <p>From RJ 67 LRH says: </p> <p>&#8220;The material involved in this sector is so vicious that it is carefully arranged to kill anyone if he discovers the exact truth of it.</p> <p>&#8220;So in January and February of this year, I became very ill, almost lost this body, and somehow or another brought it off and obtained the material, and was able to live through it. I am very sure that I was the first one that ever did live through any attempt to attain that material. This material<br /> I&#8217;m talking about, of course, is very upper level material and you will forgive me if I don&#8217;t describe it to you in very broad detail because it&#8217;s very likely to make you sick, too.</p> <p>&#8220;Now my task for the remainder of the year, up until now &#8211; which is to say the ensuing six months &#8211; was to find some way to safely bring through individuals. It was not enough for I myself to have lived through it. Other people would have to do so as well when they reached Clear and tried to move up from that point above.</p> <p>&#8220;And about five or six weeks ago, I finally was able to make a breakthrough which brought people through the zone safely. It is relatively easy to do now, provided one is an extremely well-trained auditor, and the band of fire can be walked through, bringing one out the other side unscathed, providing he applies the exact technology. No one is in danger of colliding with this at lower levels, since it concerns the formation of the society itself in which we live. A person is Clear on the first dynamic. It is necessary, to become OT, to became cleared on all dynamics, including that of society and that of the physical universe. So I have also made this breakthrough,<br /> and I don&#8217;t mind telling you, it took some doing. In all the eighteen years, this has been the toughest one that I have faced. And I faced it so that it would not be tough for you to face when you came to it.&#8221;</p> <p>You may think that the material is so out-reality for people who have not moved up to being at that level to comprehend it, or wrap their wits around it, or will get sick from being exposed to it. To those who believe that, I say you are completely underestimating and miscalculating the intelligence of common, everyday human beings. People also have the right to know what they&#8217;re buying, especially with a religious belief or subject with claims of this scope and magnitude, and thus form their own opinions and make their decisions based on that knowledge. </p> <p>I thought the pinch test was a great idea, however it&#8217;s also interesting that a new definition for what the E-Meter does was introduced by Marty- being a &#8220;truth detector.&#8221; Never heard that definition before. From what I know, all the meter really does as a device is measure resistance to the flow of current going through the body. Weather that is mental mass moving in or away, or a &#8220;body read,&#8221; all it is is a reaction to what&#8217;s happening to the flow of current. That&#8217;s it. Has nothing to do with detecting lies, or the opposite for that matter &#8211; thus making the meter itself a device of &#8220;evaluation for the pc.&#8221;</p> <p>Mike, Marty, Amy, Marc, Claire and Mareka, you all did a brilliant job to expose this dangerous Cult. It leaves this series open for further episodes IMO. You&#8217;ve got a very wide audience.</p> <p>And to Mike and Marty, I agree with others who have mentioned that just because the BBC didn&#8217;t cover a lot of the secrets you wanted exposed, you can still expose them. This blog is a great place to start. You have an audience.</p> <p>Major thumbs up!!!</p> </div>  	</div><!-- #comment-##  -->  	<ul class="children"> 	<li class="comment even depth-3 highlander-comment" id="li-comment-52625"> 		<div Unless your intent is to belittle, overwhelm or confuse the person.  And scare them away from ever studying the &#8220;scientific method&#8221; or &#8220;astrophysics&#8221;.</p> <p>As to OT III being a &#8220;major part of Scientology&#8221; &#8230; I&#8217;d say that it has its place of importance, sure (and that&#8217;s why LRH described it publicly as he did in RJ67). But the fact is, the Factors and Axioms are much more &#8220;major parts of Scientology&#8221;, and that even these don&#8217;t make much sense unless one first understands the basic books and lectures published in the 50s and 60s, before the full context or relative importance of OT III makes any sense at all.  </p> <p>If you&#8217;re afraid that &#8220;hiding a belief in entities&#8221; is a fraud and a no-no, I&#8217;d just point you to the lectures and books from the early 50s, where LRH openly discusses his views on &#8220;injected entities&#8221; and other entities in the make-up of a person.  &#8220;History of Man&#8221; comes to mind.</p> <p>This whole anti-Scn propaganda campaign to release OT III and try to belittle Scientologists and overwhelm and confuse people is just that &#8212; belittlement and propaganda.   And whether you agree with any of the data in OT III or not, I think you know enough about Scientology, the subject, to recognize that pretending that &#8220;little green martians&#8221; are the be-all and end-all of Scientology is pretty disingenuous.  In fact, it&#8217;s a lie.</p> </div>  	</div><!-- #comment-##  -->  	<ul class="children"> 	<li class="comment byuser comment-author-martyrathbun09 comment-author-is-site-member bypostauthor odd alt the early eighties, I was pretty happy when some media source brought up OT3 to disparage the church.  It was just one of those points of ridicule that became indefensible.  It put the church on its heels and could not be easily defended.  Damned if you say &#8220;yes,&#8221; damned if you say, &#8220;no.&#8221;<br /> And then to slant the whole argument to, &#8220;see what foolishness these idiots aspire to as a higher state of consciousness!  Fucking space aliens, for God&#8217;s sake!  Would you really want to study that shit?&#8221;<br /> I was furious with the church of Scientology.  Absolutely incensed that a church would have an external affairs section hell bent on destroying the lives of anyone who spoke against them.  I could have cared less what the members of a church believed as long as the members don&#8217;t believe they have the right to harm or destroy another merely for the crime of exposing a truth or voicing an opinion.<br /> It still infuriates me.<br /> As it should any person interested in understanding, personal integrity, and freedom of speech.<br /> But, to the point, the OT3 data just has that leverage, that bit of positioning which makes the church look nutty to the average viewer.  The whole thing is pretty easy to handle, as you&#8217;ve done above, but the church still hasn&#8217;t figured it out.  And the media and critics won&#8217;t let it go until the church comes up with an answer.<br /> As you&#8217;ve demonstrated, the answer will come from the Independents, when reason is applied.  Almost anyone will understand that the universe is filled with mysteries and what we&#8217;re trying to do is understand life as best we can.  Sometimes, what we find doesn&#8217;t make sense at first.  Like molecules and atoms comprised mostly of space made no sense when explaining something as solid as a brass goblet.  How could such nonsense explain something so firm and solid and strong?<br /> OT3 is merely an interesting possibility, an incidental story, not a sacred belief.  It&#8217;s like finding grandma fucking the milkman when you were six; the experience may have affected you, but you would be you with or without the experience.<br /> And Scientology would be Scientology regardless of what incidents we might or might not find in our search for truth.  The incidents are about as close to being absolutely irrelevant as anything can come to being an &#8220;absolute.&#8221;<br /> It&#8217;s the basics that are relevant.  What comprises life?  And what laws apply to those elements?<br /> Forgive my rambling.  I&#8217;m still working all this out, trying to understand, trying to assign proper importance and rearrange the furniture.<br /> So, I agree with you and thank you for the insights.</p> <p>Michael</p> </div>  	</div><!-- #comment-##  -->  	</li><!-- #comment-## --> 	<li class="comment odd alt depth-4 highlander-comment" id="li-comment-53027"> 		<div id="comment-53027"> 		<div class="comment-author vcard"> 			<img alt='' src='https://2.gravatar.com/avatar/b5ccf5df0b185252b53f035d771bf809?s=48&#038;d=identicon&#038;r=G' class='avatar avatar-48' height='48' width='48' /> 			<cite class="fn">John Peeler</cite>  			<span class="comment-meta commentmetadata"> 				| 				<a href="https://markrathbun.wordpress.com/2010/09/28/bbc-panorama-the-secrets-of-scientology/#comment-53027"> 				October 1, 2010 at 6:11 pm</a> 					| 					<a class='comment-reply-link' href='/2010/09/28/bbc-panorama-the-secrets-of-scientology/?replytocom=53027#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-53027", "53027", "respond", "3485" )' aria-label='Reply to John Peeler'>Reply</a>								</span><!-- .comment-meta .commentmetadata --> 		</div><!-- .comment-author .vcard --> 		 		<div class="comment-body"><p>Why is it that the whole time I was in Scientology, 23 years, after reading Dianetics several times, and after reading HCOB after HCOB, trained up through Class IV, as well as just making it practically a mission of mine to study the Tech for my own interest, and listen to many LRH lectures, the research behind the discoveries was never fully provided, if at all in most cases. It&#8217;s all based on someone&#8217;s &#8220;conclusions.&#8221; So, just because LRH said &#8220;This is what I came up with in my research&#8230;&#8221; we&#8217;re supposed to accept that hook line and sinker? Not me.</p> <p>From having lived through and grown up in Scientology, and after having gotten out of the CofS, I have become a realist, and someone who asks for PROOF. I know what LRH said about people who ask for proof, but I don&#8217;t care or happen to agree with that point of view. My belief in something also comes with it, how it was made to be that way. And I&#8217;m not talking about having to know what makes a car drive before buying one. Religion is NOT even close to being in the same category, especially when you&#8217;re talking about the minds of people, the answer to spirituality and the answer to life itself.</p> <p>Yes, there are positive things and workable things in Scientology, I agree, but Scientology, just by KSW alone is sold as a whole package. It&#8217;s not a buffet religion. You can&#8217;t just pick and choose what to agree and disagree with. Maybe it started out that way but then KSW came along and brought about a whole other way things must be looked at. The Study Tech even tells you that if you disagree, or don&#8217;t understand something in Scientology, you have an MU. Fucking yawn and you have an MU. Based on what?</p> <p>Believe and have faith in whatever you want. We&#8217;re lucky to have that freedom. But if you expect the rest of the world to accept Scientology as a religion or even as a valuable subject, MOST people will want the scientific proof. No joke.</p> <p>When I was a child in Scientology, it wasn&#8217;t really considered a religion BTW. But a &#8220;religious PHILOSOPHY&#8221; based on Scientific research and studies. That it was different from other religions because you didn&#8217;t have to have &#8220;faith&#8221; in something because there was a logical and scientific explanation for everything. But as it turned out, most of Scientology&#8217;s Tech is based on what LRH concluded from his own research. It would have really been nice had those research and case studies for it been fully provided. It would have also been nice if LRH had actually been a Nuclear Physicist and Medical Doctor as touted on the cover of his &#8220;All About Radiation&#8221; too.</p> <p>Let me put it this way, even in the real world, when something is being provided as scientific proof, it can absolutely be seen as real because it is fully explained and backed up by full research as to how it IS that way. It&#8217;s fail and fool proof. Real, like gravity. We don&#8217;t have to take someone&#8217;s word for it.</p> <p>I stopped taking people&#8217;s word on anything after I left. Do I need to take Obama&#8217;s word that the new health care system is gonna work just because he and his people say so? Hell no.</p> </div>  	</div><!-- #comment-##  -->  	<ul class="children"> 	<li class="comment byuser comment-author-martyrathbun09 comment-author-is-site-member bypostauthor even depth-5 highlander-comment" id="li-comment-53031"> 		<div id="comment-53031"> 		<div class="comment-author vcard"> 			<img alt='' src='https://0.gravatar.com/avatar/c2d94d163a566268e73c8b0195b6c03a?s=48&#038;d=identicon&#038;r=G' class='avatar avatar-48' height='48' width='48' /> 			<cite class="fn">martyrathbun09</cite>  			<span class="comment-meta commentmetadata"> 				| 				<a href="https://markrathbun.wordpress.com/2010/09/28/bbc-panorama-the-secrets-of-scientology/#comment-53031"> 				October 1, 2010 at 6:23 pm</a> 					| 					<a class='comment-reply-link' href='/2010/09/28/bbc-panorama-the-secrets-of-scientology/?replytocom=53031#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-53031", "53031", "respond", "3485" )' aria-label='Reply to martyrathbun09'>Reply</a>								</span><!-- .comment-meta .commentmetadata --> 		</div><!-- .comment-author .vcard --> 		 		<div class="comment-body"><p>John, your post is self contradictory. Anyone.  Doctors, psychologists,  physicists, University researchers, scientists, etc etc.</p> <p>He commented that as far as he knew no-one had taken that up.</p> <p>But  I suspect some did that,  and we just didn&#8217;t hear about it.<br /> The research we have heard about was done by government agencies who were interested in &#8220;defense&#8217; applications. I t&#8217;s al labout market share, in  their case. There&#8217;s nothing here to see&#8221;,  even as they incorporated some of the ideas and methods into their own practices.   Because maximum profits are tied to monopolize a market and be the &#8220;go to&#8221; practitioners.</p> <p>The fact is,  it would not be easy to find a truly disinterested and objective group of academics or researchers to run studies and do tests.</p> <p>As with many other things,  with auditing and training, &#8220;the proof of the pudding is in the eating.&#8221;</p> <p>If it doesn&#8217;t taste good to you,  pass on it and order something else.</p> </div>  	</div><!-- #comment-##  -->  	</li><!-- #comment-## --> </ul><!-- .children --> </li><!-- #comment-## --> </ul><!-- .children --> </li><!-- #comment-## --> 	<li class="comment odd alt depth-5 highlander-comment" id="li-comment-53114"> 		<div id="comment-53114"> 		<div class="comment-author vcard"> 			<img alt='' src='https://0.gravatar.com/avatar/35c099a407c6bcb69554239271f5ded7?s=48&#038;d=identicon&#038;r=G' class='avatar avatar-48' height='48' width='48' /> 			<cite class="fn">Margaret</cite>  			<span class="comment-meta commentmetadata"> 				| 				<a href="https://markrathbun.wordpress.com/2010/09/28/bbc-panorama-the-secrets-of-scientology/#comment-53114"> 				October 2, 2010 at 4:15 am</a> 					| 					<a class='comment-reply-link' href='/2010/09/28/bbc-panorama-the-secrets-of-scientology/?replytocom=53114#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-53114", "53114", "respond", "3485" )' aria-label='Reply to Margaret'>Reply</a>								</span><!-- .comment-meta .commentmetadata --> 		</div><!-- .comment-author .vcard --> 		 		<div class="comment-body"><p>John Peeler wrote: &#8220;Why is it that the whole time I was in Scientology, 23 years, &#8230; Those things which are uncertainties, such as metaphysics, spirits, other<br /> worlds, space opera, whole track, GE Line, are all being put into the bin called para-Scientology. The auditing we do is directed towards the establishment of certainties, and in itself works only with certainties. Prenatals, engrams and facsimiles—anything which anybody would consider uncertain does not belong on the main line.&#8221;</p> <p>&#8211; P . A . B .   N o .   2<br /> PROFESSIONAL AUDITOR’S BULLETIN<br /> From L. RON HUBBARD</p> <p>And in T H E  J O U R N A L  O F<br /> SCIENTOLOGY<br /> Issue 16-G             [1953, ca. mid-June]<br /> Published by<br /> The Hubbard Association of Scientologists, Inc.<br /> Philadelphia, Pennsylvania<br /> This is Scientology<br /> The Science of Certainty</p> <p>There are 41 entries in LRH&#8217;s works referring to Scientology as the &#8220;Science of Certainty.&#8221;</p> <p>2) &#8220;the science of knowing how to know&#8221;</p> <p>Scientology is defined as these exact words (above) in &#8230;</p> <p>A New Slant On Life<br /> Creation of Human Ability<br /> Scientology 8-8OO8<br /> Technical Dictionary<br /> Red Vol 1950-1953<br /> Red Vol 1954-1956<br /> Red Vol 1957-1959<br /> Red Vol Index</p> <p>The actual definition of Scientology used when LRH was alive is:</p> <p>SCIENTOLOGY, 1. it is formed from the Latin word scio, which means know or distinguish, being related to the word scindo, which means cleave. (Thus, the idea of differentiation is strongly implied.) It is formed from the Greek word logos, which means THE WORD, or OUTWARD FORM BY WHICH THE INWARD THOUGHT IS EXPRESSED AND MADE KNOWN: also THE INWARD THOUGHT or REASON ITSELF. Thus, SCIENTOLOGY means KNOWING ABOUT KNOWING, or SCIENCE OF KNOWLEDGE. (Scn 8-80, p. 8) 2 .   S c i e n t o l o g y  addresses the thetan. Scientology is used to increase spiritual freedom, intelligence, ability, and to produce immortality. (HCOB 22 Apr 69) 3 . an organized body of scientific research knowledge concerning life, life sources and the mind and includes practices that improve the intelligence, state and conduct of persons. (HCOB 9 Jul 59) 4 . a religious<br /> philosophy in its highest meaning as it brings man to total freedom and truth. (HCOB 18 Apr 67) 5 . the science of knowing how to know answers. It is a wisdom in the tradition of ten thousand years of search in Asia and Western civilization. It is the science of human affairs which treats the livingness and<br /> beingness of man, and demonstrates to him a pathway to greater freedom. (COHA, p. 9) 6 . an organization of the pertinencies which are mutually held true by all men in all times, and the development of technologies which demonstrate<br /> the existence of new phenomena not hitherto known, which are useful in creating states of beingness considered more desireable by man. (COHA, p. 9) 7 . the science of knowing how to know. It is the science of knowing sciences. It seeks<br /> to embrace the sciences and humanities as a clarification of knowledge itself. Into all these things—biology, physics, psychology and life itself—the skills of Scientoloa can bring order and simplification. (Scn 8-8008, p. 11) 8 . the study<br /> of the human spirit in its relationship to the physical universe and its living forms. (Abil 146)  9 . a science of life. It is the one thing senior to life because it handles all the factors of life. It contains the data necessary to live as a free being. A reality in Scientoloa is a reality on life. (Aud 27 UK) 1 0 . a body of knowledge which, when properly used, gives freedom and truth to the individual. (COHA, p. 251) 11. Scientoloa is an organized body of scientific research knowledge concerning life, life sources and the mind and includes practices that improve the<br /> intelligence, state and conduct of persons. (Abil Mi 104) 1 2 . knowledge and its application in the conquest of the material universe. (HCL 1, 5203CM03A) 1 3 . an applied philosophy designed and developed to make the able more able. In this<br /> sphere it is tremendously successful. (HCO PL 27 Oct 64) 1 4 . an applied religious philosophy dealing with the study of knowledge, which through the application of its technology, can bring about desirable changes in the conditions<br /> of life. (HCO PL 15 Apr 71R) </p> <p><b>&#8211; Dianetics and Scientology Technical Dictionary</b>(<i>Un</i>squirrelled version used when Ron was alive)</p> </div>  	</div><!-- #comment-##  -->  	</li><!-- #comment-## --> </ul><!-- .children --> </li><!-- #comment-## --> 	<li class="comment odd alt depth-5 highlander-comment" id="li-comment-53131"> 		<div id="comment-53131"> 		<div class="comment-author vcard"> 			<img alt='' src='https://2.gravatar.com/avatar/2b44c682cf154520e83c9cf7a421ad25?s=48&#038;d=identicon&#038;r=G' class='avatar avatar-48' height='48' width='48' /> 			<cite class="fn">Foremost</cite>  			<span class="comment-meta commentmetadata"> 				| 				<a href="https://markrathbun.wordpress.com/2010/09/28/bbc-panorama-the-secrets-of-scientology/#comment-53131"> 				October 2, 2010 at 5:59 am</a> 					| 					<a class='comment-reply-link' href='/2010/09/28/bbc-panorama-the-secrets-of-scientology/?replytocom=53131#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-53131", "53131", "respond", "3485" )' aria-label='Reply to Foremost'>Reply</a>								</span><!-- .comment-meta .commentmetadata --> 		</div><!-- .comment-author .vcard --> 		 		<div class="comment-body"><blockquote><p>But if you expect the rest of the world to accept Scientology as a religion or even as a valuable subject, MOST people will want the scientific proof. Heck, the coliseum is still standing.  A shadow of itself, but still there.</p> <p>The good news is there are no more slaves being led to slaughter.  No more gladiators forced to do the bidding of the depots.  No more screaming chanting crowds goading  the lions, the gladiators.</p> <p>It&#8217;s empty.  It&#8217;s a sad memory.</p> <p>Thanks to the BBC, Mike, Marty, the Headleys, Amy, Mareka, Jason and Larry &#8212; very few new people will step into an Idle Org, those in will start feeling more foolish and leave.</p> <p>On the completely unexpected side &#8230;</p> <p>&#8220;Something WONDERFUL is happening&#8221; &#8212;</p> <p>Just this past week I reconnected with two of my closest Sea Org friends.  Two wonderful souls who I haven&#8217;t spoken to in 30 years.  They left, I left, they moved, I moved and we lost touch.</p> <p>Two fabulous souls whose lives are full, happy, productive and very far from the madness we once knew.</p> <p>This reconnection happened because of this blog.</p> <p>I am so grateful.  </p> <p>WH</p> </div>  	</div><!-- #comment-##  -->  	<ul class="children"> 	<li class="comment byuser comment-author-martyrathbun09 comment-author-is-site-member bypostauthor odd alt depth-2 highlander-comment" id="li-comment-52511"> 		<div id="comment-52511"> 		<div class="comment-author vcard"> 			<img alt='' src='https://0.gravatar.com/avatar/c2d94d163a566268e73c8b0195b6c03a?s=48&#038;d=identicon&#038;r=G' class='avatar avatar-48' height='48' width='48' /> 			<cite class="fn">martyrathbun09</cite>  			<span class="comment-meta commentmetadata"> 				| 				<a href="https://markrathbun.wordpress.com/2010/09/28/bbc-panorama-the-secrets-of-scientology/#comment-52511"> 				September 29, 2010 at 2:42 pm</a> 					| 					<a class='comment-reply-link' href='/2010/09/28/bbc-panorama-the-secrets-of-scientology/?replytocom=52511#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-52511", "52511", "respond", "3485" )' aria-label='Reply to martyrathbun09'>Reply</a>								</span><!-- .comment-meta .commentmetadata --> 		</div><!-- .comment-author .vcard --> 		 		<div class="comment-body"><p>As usual, you and Just Me lend great insight and wisdom. Scientology is, consider this from  HCO PL 20 November 1965, The Promotional Actions oj&#8217; an Organization:</p> <p>&#8220;Gets pcs in such good shape they are walking advertisements for the HGC and Scientology.&#8221;</p> <p>How many of those did you see?</p> <p>On the other hand I saw a good auditor giving a pinch test which got a critic interested, a former head of OSA destimulating a critic on a past upset with the c of m and a  host of other indies that appeared very likable &#8211; yet most of them said they like Scientology and this fact was mentioned repeatedly without any denigration.</p> <p>Wonder who is an advertisement to Scientology?</p> <p>Don&#8217;t!</p> </div>  	</div><!-- #comment-##  -->  	</li><!-- #comment-## --> 	<li class="comment even thread-even depth-1 highlander-comment" id="li-comment-52502"> 		<div id="comment-52502"> 		<div class="comment-author vcard"> 			<img alt='' src='https://0.gravatar.com/avatar/35a410c5ed5cde7c7c97318a984ddcd7?s=48&#038;d=identicon&#038;r=G' class='avatar avatar-48' height='48' width='48' /> 			<cite class="fn">David from England</cite>  			<span class="comment-meta commentmetadata"> 				| 				<a href="https://markrathbun.wordpress.com/2010/09/28/bbc-panorama-the-secrets-of-scientology/#comment-52502"> 				September 29, 2010 at 2:18 pm</a> 					| 					<a class='comment-reply-link' href='/2010/09/28/bbc-panorama-the-secrets-of-scientology/?replytocom=52502#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-52502", "52502", "respond", "3485" )' aria-label='Reply to David from England'>Reply</a>								</span><!-- .comment-meta .commentmetadata --> 		</div><!-- .comment-author .vcard --> 		 		<div class="comment-body"><p>I left my initial thoughts on the programme on an earlier thread &#8211; I thought that the Independents came out as very honest decent people, and the Church as very dodgy.</p> <p>The more I think about it, and the more I read the comments here, the more I feel that this was an opportunity missed, even though it was unlikley to turn out any other way.</p> <p>By that I mean that John Sweeney  was almost obliged to make the programmme he did once Mike and Marty had blown. He had a score to settle with the Church after the &#8216;exploding tomato&#8217; incident, and what better way to get revenge than by using a defector to corroborate everything the BBC had to say the first time around, especially the spying and stalking.</p> <p>But did it tell me anything about Scientology? Not really. And although there would have been material new to some people in there, by and large it was a re-run of every critical programme since Scientology began. To me, the stand-out programme of the past few decades was Channel 4&#8217;s &#8216;Beginners Guide to L Ron Hubbard&#8217;. I say standout in the sense that it was one of the few programmes that would actually make someone more interested in scientology (note the lower case S) while being gently aware of the toxic nature of The Church. </p> <p>John  Sweeney&#8217;s film gave viewers little room to see why Scientology has been so attractive to hundreds of thousands over the decades; what we saw was a collection of shouty unattractive apologists, combined with unfairly presented Space Opera material, and a litany of (totally honest) criticisms from people cruelly treated by their church. Perhaps the only point where there was even a glimpse of the positive side to  scientology came when Marty had John on the meter &#8211; my wife (who has no interest in this matter whatsoever) was genuinely impressed at how the meter was reading something. But beyond that, it did half the job. It will keep people away from the Church. But it is unlikely to lead anyone to examine the subject of scientology further.</p> <p>I do not consider myself an ex-scientologist. I did the comm course and a few hours of auditing. I later had a run-in with the Church because I disagreed with the tech, and discovered just how disagreeable the Church can be. But  I think there is a massive amount of good in the tech that needs liberating. I see the Independent Scientologists working long and hard to uncover this good material, and I wish them the best. Programmes like this are helpful insofar as they draw people&#8217;s attention to the fact that there is an Independent movement out there.</p> <p>But I think the direction forward needs to be away from reacting to what the Church gets up  to in towards reclaiming the tech. That means more &#8216;Beginners&#8217; Guides&#8217; and less &#8216;Panorama&#8217;. It&#8217;s difficult because the Church is such an oxygen-sucking horror show, and when you can get the media interested, it&#8217;s more interested in the negative than the positive. But we do want people to see the positive. Blogs such as Marty&#8217;s do a tremdous job in this refocussing work. But on reflection, however pleased I am that Sweeney caused a little more grief for the unspeakable Tommy Davis, I don&#8217;t think that programmes such as this take the debate much further. I want to see a programme that looks at how the meter works. I want to see a programme that takes someone through auditing and out of misery into happiness. I&#8217;d like to see a programme that focuses on how the technology works. I&#8217;d like to see Independents civilly discuss with other mental health practitioners the advantages of scientology. In other words, I want to see scientology come out of its self-imposed ghetto and relate to the outside world once more.</p> <p>Right now the Church is talking to itself. I think that Indies offer scientology its only chance to actually engage with the world. For that, the spiral has to be broken &#8211; Indies need to be able to present their work on its own terms, not as a &#8216;cleaned up&#8217; response to the excesses of te Miscavage empire.</p> <p>I realise how difficult this is, and I realise that the Church will do anything to stop this. But my feeling is that this is the best way forward.</p> </div>  	</div><!-- #comment-##  -->  	<ul class="children"> 	<li class="comment byuser comment-author-martyrathbun09 comment-author-is-site-member bypostauthor odd alt depth-2 highlander-comment" id="li-comment-52505"> 		<div id="comment-52505"> 		<div class="comment-author vcard"> 			<img alt='' src='https://0.gravatar.com/avatar/c2d94d163a566268e73c8b0195b6c03a?s=48&#038;d=identicon&#038;r=G' class='avatar avatar-48' height='48' width='48' /> 			<cite class="fn">martyrathbun09</cite>  			<span class="comment-meta commentmetadata"> 				| 				<a href="https://markrathbun.wordpress.com/2010/09/28/bbc-panorama-the-secrets-of-scientology/#comment-52505"> 				September 29, 2010 at 2:25 pm</a> 					| 					<a class='comment-reply-link' href='/2010/09/28/bbc-panorama-the-secrets-of-scientology/?replytocom=52505#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-52505", "52505", "respond", "3485" )' aria-label='Reply to martyrathbun09'>Reply</a>								</span><!-- .comment-meta .commentmetadata --> 		</div><!-- .comment-author .vcard --> 		 		<div class="comment-body"><p>David, I believe you are right on the money. The problem with protest blogs and journalistic / scholarly criticism is that important elements such as purpose, intention and reality factor are often left on the editing floor.   The same is true for rabid criticism and rabid fanaticism.  </p> <p>All too often I see snips of LRH materials quoted to carry an argument &#8212; the are taken out of context both in terms of surrounding or later materials and in terms of the time period in which they were written.  There is little regard for the possibility that one&#8217;s viewpoint can and does change over time through experience and new knowledge, through fundamental changes in tone level &#8211; to name a few things.  I have always been surprised to find that I can read the same materials from a new viewpoint / insight that I gained from auditing or just living life and find that my understanding of it has changed.  Often quite markedly.  </p> <p>IMO the most important message is that this information cannot be ENFORCED on people.  You can&#8217;t MAKE someone better.  You can MAKE them behave in a different way by using FORCE but you cannot produce reason by using FORCE.  One of my greatest challenges over the years has been dealing with staff members who want to HELP me by enforcing their viewpoint and interpretations on me by saying something along the lines of &#8220;LRH says&#8230;&#8221;  Indeed, LRH said a lot of things.  Millions of words in fact, so many that you can&#8217;t possibly jump in with LRH says in a pet quote.  Losing sight of the changes over time, the events occurring at the time, the problems being addressed, the overarching principles and underlying fundamentals has led to this ridiculous point of view of LRH as a demi-god and the research / discussion / training materials and lectures found in the books and tapes  as &#8220;scriptures&#8221; to be followed &#8220;or else.&#8221;  &#8220;Or else&#8221; is just enforcement, is a violation of core principles and I believe it is the primary reason for the disastrous state of the C of S.</p> </div>  	</div><!-- #comment-##  -->  	<ul class="children"> 	<li class="comment odd alt depth-3 highlander-comment" id="li-comment-52822"> 		<div id="comment-52822"> 		<div class="comment-author vcard"> 			<img alt='' src='https://0.gravatar.com/avatar/35c099a407c6bcb69554239271f5ded7?s=48&#038;d=identicon&#038;r=G' class='avatar avatar-48' height='48' width='48' /> 			<cite class="fn">Margaret</cite>  			<span class="comment-meta commentmetadata"> 				| 				<a href="https://markrathbun.wordpress.com/2010/09/28/bbc-panorama-the-secrets-of-scientology/#comment-52822"> 				September 30, 2010 at 8:57 pm</a> 					| 					<a class='comment-reply-link' href='/2010/09/28/bbc-panorama-the-secrets-of-scientology/?replytocom=52822#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-52822", "52822", "respond", "3485" )' aria-label='Reply to Margaret'>Reply</a>								</span><!-- .comment-meta .commentmetadata --> 		</div><!-- .comment-author .vcard --> 		 		<div class="comment-body"><p>Another excellent post Maria. wrong with the church of scientology?</p> <p>From what I&#8217;ve seen and personally experienced it is this:</p> <p>     Every being in this universe is unique, there is only one of you and there is only one of me. Instead of treating people for what they really are, which is unique and irreplaceable beings in this universe, in my opinion, they are seen as just another mark or just another slave.</p> <p>     To me this is a business mentality and not the correct way of looking at things when one is trying to reverse the effects of being in this universe for billions of years.</p> </div>  	</div><!-- #comment-##  -->  	</li><!-- #comment-## --> 	<li class="comment odd alt thread-odd thread-alt depth-1 highlander-comment" id="li-comment-52541"> 		<div id="comment-52541"> 		<div class="comment-author vcard"> 			<img alt='' src='https://2.gravatar.com/avatar/2fb4b1135fe28557060ab78b6f1f42b7?s=48&#038;d=identicon&#038;r=G' class='avatar avatar-48' height='48' width='48' /> 			<cite class="fn"><a href='http://leavingscientology' rel='external nofollow' class='url'>OnceUponaTime</a></cite>  			<span class="comment-meta commentmetadata"> 				| 				<a href="https://markrathbun.wordpress.com/2010/09/28/bbc-panorama-the-secrets-of-scientology/#comment-52541"> 				September 29, 2010 at 3:51 pm</a> 					| 					<a class='comment-reply-link' href='/2010/09/28/bbc-panorama-the-secrets-of-scientology/?replytocom=52541#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-52541", "52541", "respond", "3485" )' aria-label='Reply to OnceUponaTime'>Reply</a>								</span><!-- .comment-meta .commentmetadata --> 		</div><!-- .comment-author .vcard --> 		 		<div class="comment-body"><p>I had time to watch one segment and ended up watching them all.  Thought the feature was compelling.  </p> <p>Maybe the disappointment lies more in expectations:  like being told a movie is the best things ever, sitting through it and thinking, &#8220;Hmm, not that great.&#8221;  Or being told a movie is the worst thing ever, sitting through it and thinking, &#8220;Hmm, not that bad, had some good parts.&#8221;</p> <p>The intrusiveness of the church was manifest in the ubiquitous cameras.  The lies and betrayals came through loud and clear.  All the attempts to intimidate, the spiked fences, Tommy&#8217;s nastiness.  As Sweeny asked, &#8220;Is this how this church goes about its business?&#8221;</p> <p>Look at the &#8220;missed opportunity&#8221; in a different way:  a thetan loves a mystery.  A good writer does not provide too much information too early in the story.  The author wants the reader to continue to turn the page, to be compelled to find out.  Maybe this will get some to research further who had not thought to do so before.</p> <p>That the material was often a rehash of what we&#8217;ve seen before is less important than it serving as a continued message.  Certainly we here on this blog have seen it all before.  But others have not.  And even if they have, a study datum says that number of times over material equals certainty and results.  The audience is learning.  This program may be the moment of revelation, when the data actually gets through, past the denial and the apathy.  This organization needs to be handled.  </p> <p>Michael</p> </div>  	</div><!-- #comment-##  -->  	<ul class="children"> 	<li class="comment byuser comment-author-martyrathbun09 It wasn&#8217;t the wisdom.  It wasn&#8217;t the comm course.  It wasn&#8217;t the idea of going clear.  It wasn&#8217;t the idea of saving the planet.  It was the good-looking women.  </p> <p>Nothing like a beautiful woman to set my heart thumping.  </p> <p>No wonder advertiser use those images.  Within a week of starting the comm course I had paid for training through level four and auditing through OT3&#8211;just because the reg was so damned cute.  </p> <p>So, maybe next lifetime, when my head is clear, my heart pure and my motives noble, I will return to lend service to humanity.  But, for now&#8230;  Ah!  My heart is set to thumping.</p> <p>And regardless of my initial motivation, I&#8217;ve learned a few things along the way.  And met lots of friends.  People I truly enjoy. We can share our thoughts and give our support without fear of repercussion.  </p> <p>That which motivates us varies from individual to individual.  But each has so much to contribute, both here and with one another.   Great religions spread by word of mouth, not by corporate finesse.  It will be our words, our mouths, by which Scientology will spread.  </p> <p>We are the emissaries of a philosophy.  We are the lovers of wisdom.</p> <p>Ain&#8217;t it a bitch?</p> <p>Michael</p> </div>  	</div><!-- #comment-##  -->  	<ul class="children"> 	<li class="comment even depth-2 highlander-comment" Hearing the profane screams directed at Mike by his family in the parking lot was frightening (and saddening). </p> <p>I also thought the fact that Sweeney included the boilerplate CofM denial every time he presented credible evidence of a CofM atrocity or outrage had to have been very damaging to CofM. Every fact was presented either by direct video or stated by a very credible witness (and all came across as such, to their great credit). </p> <p>To have obvious facts denied over &amp; over communicated clearly that CofM is a scary organization, one that is running amok in society, unaccountable, attempting to intimidate anyone who disagrees with them. </p> <p>I&#8217;m no newbie &amp; by now I&#8217;m well aware of what has been and is going on &#8211; and yet, I experienced chills as I watched this program. I can only imagine what impression the average viewer came away with. It cannot have been anything but devastating for DM and his dwindling band of not so merry men (and women).</p> <p>As others have remarked, the tear coming down Mareka&#8217;s cheek at the end created the most profound impact of all. Seeing that made me choke up. What a terrible thing to do to another human being. And to LRH&#8217;s legacy. These people who have hijacked our church are THUGS and they MUST be stopped.</p> </div>  	</div><!-- #comment-##  -->  	<ul class="children"> 	<li class="comment odd alt depth-2 highlander-comment" id="li-comment-52865"> 		<div id="comment-52865"> 		<div class="comment-author vcard"> 			<img alt='' src='https://0.gravatar.com/avatar/f0fada286f456827d2daf5a5109e370a?s=48&#038;d=identicon&#038;r=G' class='avatar avatar-48' height='48' width='48' /> 			<cite class="fn">Wayne Froemke (AKA "Safe")</cite>  			<span class="comment-meta commentmetadata"> 				| 				<a href="https://markrathbun.wordpress.com/2010/09/28/bbc-panorama-the-secrets-of-scientology/#comment-52865"> 				September 30, 2010 at 11:51 pm</a> 					| 					<a class='comment-reply-link' href='/2010/09/28/bbc-panorama-the-secrets-of-scientology/?replytocom=52865#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-52865", "52865", "respond", "3485" )' aria-label='Reply to Wayne Froemke (AKA &quot;Safe&quot;)'>Reply</a>								</span><!-- .comment-meta .commentmetadata --> 		</div><!-- .comment-author .vcard --> 		 		<div class="comment-body"><p>Publius wrote, &#8220;These people who have hijacked our church are THUGS and they MUST be stopped.&#8221;</p> <p>Excellent comment, Publius.</p> <p>Essentially, we&#8217;ve had THUGS hijack the CofS, and use it for profit, to demand admiration, and to control other bodies (commit slavery).</p> <p>What Scientologist would have ever imagined that a BULLY would end up becoming the &#8220;Great Leader&#8221; This weeks&#8217; edition of popular fortnightly satirical magazine &#8220;Private Eye&#8221; carried a piece about Scientology and the Panorama documentary in its occasional column &#8220;Cult Corner&#8221;.  I couldn&#8217;t find any way of sending you a scanned copy (fair enough; am guessing you&#8217;d be constantly spammed if you put your email address on here), so have typed it out for you.  Here it is:<br /> &#8220;&#8216; YOU suck cock on Hollywood Boulevard.&#8221; This is the word of the Church of Scientology, according to its former spokesman Mike Rinder, who spilled the beans in John Sweeney&#8217;s BBC film this week.<br /> He was citing a text message sent from the office of the leader, David Miscavige, Tom Cruise&#8217;s best man – one of many bizarre obscenities, Rinder claims. After half a century inside the church, Rinder now says that it is a cult.</p> <p>But some public figures in Britain are still happy to give it the benefit of the doubt. &#8220;I don&#8217;t think Scientologists get a fair deal,&#8221; Jonathan Ross wrote in his autobiography. When Tom Cruise repaid the favour by appearing on Ross&#8217;s show, the sycophantic host gave him a very fair deal indeed by not asking about Scientology at all.</p> <p>Another admirer is the coalition&#8217;s new minister for climate change, Charles Hendry, a Tory MP whose seat borders the 59-acre Scientology estate in East Grinstead. In 2004 Hendry attended the premiere of Tom Cruise&#8217;s film Collateral. &#8220;I thought Tom was absolutely amazing,&#8221; he gushed. When the star chatted to Hendry&#8217;s stepdaughter on the MP&#8217;s mobile phone, Hendry said: &#8220;Clare thought it was the coolest thing ever.&#8221; A year later, in July 2005, Hendry told the House of Commons: &#8220;Although Scientology may be very controversial&#8230; undoubtedly as human beings they do a great deal of good&#8230; certainly as an organisation it&#8217;s gone through serious hoops in terms of making sure it has the right to broadcast on TV, satisfying the broadcasting commission that it isn&#8217;t a cult.&#8221;</p> <p>The &#8220;broadcasting commission&#8221; is a reference to the Independent Television Commission, which has since been succeeded by Ofcom.  Neither body was in a position to say whether the church was or was not a cult, and neither did. But Judge Latey in the high court in 1984 called it exactly that: &#8220;a cult&#8230; corrupt, sinister and dangerous&#8230; out to capture people and&#8230; brainwash them.&#8221;</p> <p>In Britain, the church operates as the Church of Scientology Religious Educational College Inc. a not-for-profit organisation which filed an income of L12,958,196 in 2008. Despite its wealth, and the Charity Commission&#8217;s ruling that the church isn&#8217;t a charity for religious purposes, the City of London Corporation grants 80 percent rates relief for its &#8220;London Org&#8221; (ie HQ) on Queen Victoria Street, thus saving it a total of L1,306,363 in rates since the centre opened in 2006. Westminster city council gives 80 percent rate relief on its &#8220;London Celebrity Centre&#8221; in Leinster Gardens, saving it L165,303 over the past decade. Birmingham city council gives 80 percent rates relief on the Scientology property at Winston Churchill House, as does Sunderland council at the new L5m &#8220;Org&#8221; on Fawcett Street. Whether the church enjoys rates relief on the most famous Scientology property in Britain, its &#8220;stress test centre&#8221; on Tottenham Court Road, is a secret: Camden council refuses to answer questions on the subject.</p> <p>A few brave local authorities haven&#8217;t yet been brainwashed. Manchester city council charges the full commercial rate on the L5m &#8220;Org&#8221; in Deansgate. as does Mid-Sussex district council for the estate at Saint Hill Manor near East Grinstead. With a government minister on the Scientologists&#8217; side, however, can it be long before the dissenting councils cave in to Tom Cruise&#8217;s creepy church?</p> <p>• PS: Further proof of the Scientologists&#8217; wealth is the fact that their solicitors sent the BBC hundreds of letters, running to 1,100 pages in all, while Sweeney was preparing his latest film. Since the solicitors in question are Carter- Fuck &#8211; take a bow, partner Alasdair Pepper &#8211; the bill is unlikely to be much less than Llm.&#8221;<br /> (N.B. &#8216;Carter-Fuck&#8217; is how Private Eye always refers to the London law firm Carter-Ruck).  I can send you a scanned version, if you prefer.<br /> Peace,<br /> IEG x</p> </div>  	</div><!-- #comment-##  -->  	</li><!-- #comment-## --> 	<li class="comment odd alt thread-even depth-1 highlander-comment" id="li-comment-52799"> 		<div id="comment-52799"> 		<div class="comment-author vcard"> 			<img alt='' src='https://0.gravatar.com/avatar/96c878df67231f107c1293efba8ffb7c?s=48&#038;d=identicon&#038;r=G' class='avatar avatar-48' height='48' width='48' /> 			<cite class="fn">sarge</cite>  			<span class="comment-meta commentmetadata"> 				| 				<a href="https://markrathbun.wordpress.com/2010/09/28/bbc-panorama-the-secrets-of-scientology/#comment-52799"> 				September 30, 2010 at 6:10 pm</a> 					| 					<a class='comment-reply-link' href='/2010/09/28/bbc-panorama-the-secrets-of-scientology/?replytocom=52799#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-52799", "52799", "respond", "3485" )' aria-label='Reply to sarge'>Reply</a>								</span><!-- .comment-meta .commentmetadata --> 		</div><!-- .comment-author .vcard --> 		 		<div class="comment-body"><p>Marty, After seeing the Panorama videos and reading most of the comments here I have to agree that it was a very good expose&#8217; on<br /> the Church of Scientology. I’d just like to try to paint a picture for you of how different the Church of Scientology used to be compared to today and why it is that Marty’s auditor behavior appeared to be so safe when you saw him on TV showing John Sweeney how the e-meter worked.  </p> <p>I was a public member of the Church from 1972 through 1988 and spent many, many hours on both sides of the meter – I’m OT4 and Class 4.  From those years I don’t recall a single time an auditor or a word clearer or a qual person or an ethics officer tried intentionally to make me wrong or harass me or invalidate me or f**k with me in any way.  </p> <p>To illustrate, here’s a story that may out me to some lurkers.  Before I was in Scientology I practiced Transcendental Meditation.  In TM you’re given a mantra and agree to never reveal your mantra.  (Since then many times I’ve seen my TM mantra printed in mainstream magazines and newspapers, so it’s not really a secret anymore.)  But once in an auditing session the subject of my TM participation and my confidential mantra came up.  My auditor, seeking details, asked what my mantra was.  I said, “Sorry!  That’s confidential.  I agreed to keep my mantra a secret.  Not telling!”  And my auditor said, “Thank you very much, your needle’s floating.  Ok, now we’ll take up the subject of ….” And that was the end of that.  </p> <p>Because you see – THAT’s the way auditing is supposed to go.  One’s own upsets, problems, withholds and the much more interesting things one addresses in auditing are defined and evaluated by the preclear, NOT by the auditor.   The auditor’s job is to get the preclear into session, ask questions, listen to answers, acknowledge and basically get the hell out of the way.  And, of course, sort things out if things get tangled up or too complicated.  But when the auditor starts interrupting and drawing attention to themselves or being interested in something the preclear has no interest in or telling the preclear that they’re wrong about their perceptions, then the session has gone kaput!  That’s not auditing.  I don’t know what that is, but again it’s not auditing.  </p> <p>This past year I’ve been astonished to understand the bizarre changes that have taken place in the Co$ since I left it for reasons having to do with the Scientology organization, especially its money-for-status aspects.  All these stories of heavy-handed sec-checking and black Dianetics and reverse Scientology are still slightly unreal to me – only because I was never subjected to them.  But I absolutely believe the people who are telling these horror stories.</p> <p>So if you hear some of us whinging on and on about the ‘tech’ – it’s because we learned about Scientology when it was simply about helping people become more able and explore the bigger Mysteries of Life and our own smaller lives.  I think you would have had to have loved the subject and experienced its effectiveness to now be so appalled by how it has been diluted and destroyed inside the Church to serve the need for greed and power and insanity of a few.  </p> <p>And before anyone else says it – I know, tl; dr.  </p> <p>Just Me</p> </div>  	</div><!-- #comment-##  -->  	<ul class="children"> 	<li class="comment byuser I especially liked your last sentence &#8211; anyone reading that would have to come away with a much better understanding of why those of us who are so loyal to the tech are so appalled by what has happened.</p> <p>My track overlaps yours and I agree with everything you say about the scene as it was during much of that time. I would only add that I spent a lot of time at Flag from 1989 to 1996, and during those years, it was also all about helping people become more able. I looked forward to every trip I took to Flag. The staff I dealt with, were some of the friendliest, most helpful, most competent people I&#8217;ve ever known (the exceptions being the ever-present reges, but I never really had much difficulty figuring out ways to avoid them). </p> <p>The services I received, whether training or auditing, were superb. I ALWAYS left Flag feeling like I&#8217;d had a &#8220;spiritual shower&#8221;, ready to tackle life from a much better place. It was a wonderful time. The slogan &#8220;The Friendliest Place in the Whole World&#8221; really meant something then &#8211; it was not just a slogan, it was the truth.</p> <p>Then in 1996, it all changed. It was like a bunch of aliens came in &amp; took over. Kind of like those aliens in &#8220;V&#8221; if you&#8217;ve seen that show &#8211; human on the outside, reptiles on the inside. That was the end for me.</p> <p>As happy as it makes me to contemplate the growth of an independent Scientology movement, it also saddens me to think that the present church is probably beyond reform. That means no more Flag as I knew it. And what becomes of St. Hill Manor? These are to some degree MEST concerns, but there was at one time a lot of theta connected with these and other places in Scientology&#8217;s history.  </p> <p>David Miscavige has so much to answer for.</p> </div>  	</div><!-- #comment-##  -->  	</li><!-- #comment-## --> </ul><!-- .children --> </li><!-- #comment-## --> 	<li class="comment even depth-5 highlander-comment" id="li-comment-52873"> 		<div id="comment-52873"> 		<div class="comment-author vcard"> 			<img alt='' src='https://2.gravatar.com/avatar/2fb4b1135fe28557060ab78b6f1f42b7?s=48&#038;d=identicon&#038;r=G' class='avatar avatar-48' height='48' width='48' /> 			<cite class="fn"><a href='http://leavingscientology.wordpress.com' rel='external nofollow' class='url'>OnceUponaTime</a></cite>  			<span class="comment-meta commentmetadata"> 				| 				<a href="https://markrathbun.wordpress.com/2010/09/28/bbc-panorama-the-secrets-of-scientology/#comment-52873"> 				October 1, 2010 at 12:30 am</a> 					| 					<a class='comment-reply-link' href='/2010/09/28/bbc-panorama-the-secrets-of-scientology/?replytocom=52873#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-52873", "52873", "respond", "3485" )' aria-label='Reply to OnceUponaTime'>Reply</a>								</span><!-- .comment-meta .commentmetadata --> 		</div><!-- .comment-author .vcard --> 		 		<div class="comment-body"><p>Impartial,</p> <p>Your two cents are worth two cents, but properly invested, who the fuck knows how much they&#8217;re worth. We want to see happiness and success if it is genuine. We all know that people are not 100% successful all of the time, nor are we 100% happy all of the time. A sincere communication won&#8217;t ignore those realities. But, if the message is too unrealistic, we tend to dismiss it as advertising.</p> <p>There&#8217;s a bumper sticker that says &#8220;I&#8217;m a Christian under construction&#8221;. What it&#8217;s trying to communicate is &#8211; I know I don&#8217;t get it right all the time, but I think I&#8217;m headed in the right direction. (Whether it successfully communicates that I leave to you.)</p> <p>I guess I&#8217;m encouraging Indies to be &#8220;real&#8221; with people when you&#8217;re promoting your faith. No one expects perfection. Rather, a mature person is able to acknowledge their growth areas and to celebrate that they are actually growing, even if they aren&#8217;t yet where they aim to be.</p> </div>  	</div><!-- #comment-##  -->  	</li><!-- #comment-## --> </ul><!-- .children --> </li><!-- #comment-## --> 	<li class="comment even depth-2 highlander-comment" id="li-comment-52843"> 		<div id="comment-52843"> 		<div class="comment-author vcard"> 			<img alt='' src='https://2.gravatar.com/avatar/8c30eacbdfa2575bc18680b2579b5e2b?s=48&#038;d=identicon&#038;r=G' class='avatar avatar-48' height='48' width='48' /> 			<cite class="fn">veritas</cite>  			<span class="comment-meta commentmetadata"> 				| 				<a href="https://markrathbun.wordpress.com/2010/09/28/bbc-panorama-the-secrets-of-scientology/#comment-52843"> 				September 30, 2010 at 10:33 pm</a> 					| 					<a class='comment-reply-link' href='/2010/09/28/bbc-panorama-the-secrets-of-scientology/?replytocom=52843#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-52843", "52843", "respond", "3485" )' aria-label='Reply to veritas'>Reply</a>								</span><!-- .comment-meta .commentmetadata --> 		</div><!-- .comment-author .vcard --> 		 		<div class="comment-body"><p>The BBC show  &#8220;The Secrets of Scientology&#8221; was a successful expose on the sinister intimidation, in action.   Even though the show documented only a small tip of the iceberg, the modus operandi of the organization calling itself the &#8220;Church of Scientology&#8221; has been correctly observed and spotlighted.</p> <p>I find it important to note that the show did include coverage about the infamous text messages from the Office of the COB to his &#8220;church&#8221; staff, berating and invalidating dedicated Sea Org executives with obscenities.  This is significant because, even though the Organization of Scientology issued a statement that these text messgaes &#8220;could have been&#8221; (ooo loophole mania)   &#8220;forgeries&#8221;, and BBC dutifully included their soundbyte   statement,  one can surmise there is ample proof 1). these abusive text messages are in fact genuine, that the obscene insults were indeed texted from David Miscavige&#8217;s phone and 2) the office was in charge of and aware of  people who were off on intimidation and surveillance missions. to undermine and destroy.</p> <p> The text messages can be verified and proved. They are on record in actual phones and with the phone providers.  BBC obviously did their homework, and by verifying and reporting on the abusive texting and  surveillance  orders/games from the Office of COB,  proved validity of at least one of the many complaints of people leaving, i.e., verbal abuse and unethical abuse of power.     In they process, this simultaneously spotlighted the Organization as Habitual Liars.     And offers more credibility to some ground, i.e. &#8220;the secrets left on the cutting room floor&#8221;, that have yet to come to light, but for legal and practical reasons were circumvented.</p> <p>This abuse of people serving ideals and the betterment of life is deeply tragic and disappointing.  The abuse of persons asking for help is, bar none,  one of the most heinous travesties possible against human decency.</p> <p>My sentiments seeing this show were mixed: triumph for truth, justice, sadness, loss, admiration and &#8230;hope.    I admired everyone who communicated.  It was notable how much more radiant and well the Independent Scientologists are than those &#8220;inside.&#8221;  </p> <p>The operation of the trademarked brand Scientology emerges as sinister, abusive, and dishonest and run by a megolomaniac playing with people&#8217;s lives and black SUVS as though they were a Tonka toy collection pitted against make-believe (delusion or play, choose)  enemies.   It emerges this way not because of any bias a media reporter might have (wrong target), but because of the <i>proven documentation</i> of habitual, repeated transgressions against the mores of society and code of human decency &#8212; not to mention looking like a bunch of unenlightened, sickly  sourpusses.  </p> <p>I&#8217;m not saying this to be mean.  Come on! These are NOT the poster children for enlightenment. It was sad to see so many unhappy, uptight people.     However, it is not because of Scientology.   This is the tricky illusion that public awareness needs to grasp!  The irony is that people <i>outside</i>  the &#8220;Church&#8221;  are using the actual subject of Sceintology as it was developed and for the purposes it was intended, i.e. help and self-help. </p> <p>While the spotlight BBC directed toward  unconscionable and irresponsible behavior by a US Corporation was laudable, courageous, cutting edge journalism and successful,   I was very disappointed by the comic book representation of the intergalactic warlord .   </p> <p>Unlike others, I&#8217;m not offended by it, I&#8217;m merely disappointed at the inaccuracy of the depiction and hope this does not undermine the validity of excellent reporting, i.e. being the eyes of the world and all the duties and protocol of objectivity that entails.     The first inaccuracy about the outerspace stuff is that it this is touted as the crux of Scientology &#8212; it is not! The depiction is understandable from one POV (point of view):  it&#8217;s easier to wrap one&#8217;s mind around a cartoon in 30 seconds media time!  And we all love a good laugh.  And it is an easy, cheap shot at ceritfying some who would believe such a thing as nutty.   Right? </p> <p>I personally think good reporting broke down in that spot.  All that journalism would have required to fix that hole would have been the inclusion, even if brief and summarized, of the broader spectrum of the subject of Scientology, and also a brief parallel of similarity and differences of other religions as a comparison.  </p> <p>Here&#8217;s an example of how I think it failed:  The comic book illustrated sound-byte of &#8220;what Scientologists believe&#8221;  would be the same as if a show about the abuses of the Vatican, for example, depicted the Christian practice of Holy Mass as a cannibalistic ritual by people thinking they were drinking real blood and eating flesh of a man named Jesus Christ.   Yikes! There&#8217;s some iota of truth there, but it does not make it accurate.     The other disservice done by such a depiction would be that Mass is only one of many sacraments and  rituals practiced.</p> <p>But besides, a way that Scientology differs from many religions is that it is not based on beliefs.   </p> <p>My point is not to discuss Holy Communion as a metaphor, nor is it to examine the validity of any ritual a person chooses to employ that serves as a solution and instrument for betterment or understanding of existence and Life.   These are largely personal matters.</p> <p>Where religion stops being a personal matter to respect in others is where it crosses the line into intrusion and abuse of people.  Then it becomes public.   And that is what the BBC has successfully platformed.  I can only hope the public at large can differentiate between the subject.    The reality is that most people already <i>do</i> make the distinction between spirituality and religion.  Why?  Because religions have a history of being hijacked and altered for personal gain by delusional and corrupt dictators.  So I don&#8217;t think it&#8217;s too big a leap for viewers watching the show to make.</p> <p>Yes,  it&#8217;s somewhat primitive to see a subject I understand, such as Scientology, a subject that holds merit and is efficient, be  reduced to a few yuks of a media sound-byte&#8230;but I&#8217;m not going to pull an Anne Archer over it;)  lol      </p> <p>As for life on other planets,  hey, yestedray the first Earth-like planet revolving a sun was discovered, and the astrophysicist who discovered it states he&#8217;s 100% sure it has the conditions for Life. </p> <p>I hope to see many discussions about Scientology and the nature of life amongst well-meaning people.</p> </div>  	</div><!-- #comment-##  -->  	<ul class="children"> 	<li class="comment byuser The depiction is understandable from one POV (point of view): it’s easier to wrap one’s mind around a cartoon in 30 seconds media time! And we all love a good laugh. And it is an easy, cheap shot at ceritfying some who would believe such a thing as nutty. Right? </i></p> <p>V, here&#8217;s why I think non-Scientologists will often say that OTIII is the crux of Scientology:</p> <p>1) In the Judeo-Christian religions, the book of Genesis &#8211; and particularly the first 3 chapters &#8211; form the foundation. There we learn who we are in relation to God and all of creation. There we learn who we are! We are created, not the Creator. But we alone among creation have been made &#8220;in the image of&#8221; God (Imago Dei). That means there is something about the human that is like God. Like God, we are spiritual beings. Like God, we are creative. Etc.</p> <p>When people from western cultures come at religion, it is natural for them to want the scientology equivalent of genesis.  And subconsciously, the probably means they expect a STORY that answers some of the biggest quesitons. ie. Who does Scientology say we are? What does Scientology say about God? </p> <p>OTIII is a story and it is the closest thing people have seen to being Scientology&#8217;s genesis.</p> <p>2) OTIII was given power because it was made mysterious and called &#8220;the Wall of Fire&#8221;.  </p> <p>3) The church did not explain what IS the crux of scientology.  The boilerplate &#8220;Man is a spiritual being &#8230; (yada) &#8230; visit an org, buy a book&#8221; is really a non-explanation.  It leaves a vacuum that is still not filled. </p> <p>So while OTIII does cause a lot of mirth, I do not think that those labelling it the crux of scientology do so with any ill intent. Or at least, I can see how they could very innocently reach that conclusion.</p> </div>  	</div><!-- #comment-##  -->  	<ul class="children"> 	<li class="comment odd alt depth-4 highlander-comment" id="li-comment-53003"> 		<div id="comment-53003"> 		<div class="comment-author vcard"> 			<img alt='' src='https://0.gravatar.com/avatar/3b7ce26a18fece865bf84652fbc083cc?s=48&#038;d=identicon&#038;r=G' class='avatar avatar-48' height='48' width='48' /> 			<cite class="fn">Grasshopper</cite>  			<span class="comment-meta commentmetadata"> 				| 				<a href="https://markrathbun.wordpress.com/2010/09/28/bbc-panorama-the-secrets-of-scientology/#comment-53003"> 				October 1, 2010 at 3:33 pm</a> 					| 					<a class='comment-reply-link' href='/2010/09/28/bbc-panorama-the-secrets-of-scientology/?replytocom=53003#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-53003", "53003", "respond", "3485" )' aria-label='Reply to Grasshopper'>Reply</a>								</span><!-- .comment-meta .commentmetadata --> 		</div><!-- .comment-author .vcard --> 		 		<div class="comment-body"><p>OT III is one level of many. There were seventeen years between 1950 and 1967. Virtually all of Scientology was researched and released before OT III. The &#8220;crux&#8221; of Scientology, the Genesis, if you will, is in the Logics, the Factors, the Axioms, and the Theta-MEST theory from Science of Survival, not OT III. </p> <p>OT III could be considered to be a commonly shared experience for some people. While important, it is not fundamental. I spent sixteen very productive and enlightened years in Scientology before I did OT III. I had a lot of gain on OT III as mentioned above. But I got much, much more from the fundamentals I listed above than I did from OT III. </p> <p>Your point 2 above is correct &#8211; if it wasn&#8217;t under wraps, it would not be such a prize for journalists. I often wondered why the History of Man stories were not more publicized. Perhaps because it was out in the open. </p> <p>Your point 3 is very valid. I huge flaw in the church is that people will not answer questions &#8211; when they should. &#8220;What is Scientology?&#8221; &#8220;Here, read this!&#8221; &#8220;Here, read  this!&#8221; is not a real answer. It is part of the answer, but not the only answer. So, naturally, when there is a vacuum of information, people will fill it with whatever they can find.</p> </div>  	</div><!-- #comment-##  -->  	<ul class="children"> 	<li class="comment even depth-5 highlander-comment" id="li-comment-54282"> 		<div id="comment-54282"> 		<div class="comment-author vcard"> 			<img alt='' src='https://2.gravatar.com/avatar/e4b4bbe3e09f5e00c8061846bd634296?s=48&#038;d=identicon&#038;r=G' class='avatar avatar-48' height='48' width='48' /> 			<cite class="fn">Heather G</cite>  			<span class="comment-meta commentmetadata"> 				| 				<a href="https://markrathbun.wordpress.com/2010/09/28/bbc-panorama-the-secrets-of-scientology/#comment-54282"> 				October 6, 2010 at 11:30 am</a> 					| 					<a class='comment-reply-link' href='/2010/09/28/bbc-panorama-the-secrets-of-scientology/?replytocom=54282#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-54282", "54282", "respond", "3485" )' aria-label='Reply to Heather G'>Reply</a>								</span><!-- .comment-meta .commentmetadata --> 		</div><!-- .comment-author .vcard --> 		 		<div class="comment-body"><p>I hear you, Grasshopper. It really is. It shows the passing of the baton of real Scientology from the church, to the Reformers. I&#8217;d love to hear your takes on this, but I really think that is the case.</p> <p>I was thinking &#8211; when I was younger, and something weird would happen when I was on staff or on course, I would think to myself &#8211; &#8220;That&#8217;s not Scientology.&#8221; Since I was trained well at an early age, I knew enough to know what was and what was not &#8220;kosher&#8221; from a tech point of view.</p> <p>When I saw shows on TV (the ABC show in 1976 was  the first I really noticed, but then there was 60 minutes and other shows), I would not recognize what the show was passing off as Scientology.
